Stage 6 Primer ‚Äî RuberuTutor Secondary (Grades 9‚Äì12)
0) Repo Truths (don‚Äôt drift)

Authoritative sources: Ontario curriculum PDFs/Word snapshots only; copy verbatim expectations and codes. # A) Create from template
cp curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/_TEMPLATE_SECONDARY_MAP.md curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/COURSECODE.md

Tip: Set source_pdf: to the exact file you commit under curriculum/ontario/‚Ä¶pdf.

4) Pulling Verbatim Expectations (safe workflow)

Open the official PDF (Ontario curriculum).

Copy strand Overall then Specific expectations into the map.

Keep codes, punctuation, spelling exactly as in the PDF.

Add a short commit per block (Strand A, then B, etc.)‚Äîfast and auditable.

Commit examplesMaps live at: curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/

Worksheets: materials/worksheets/{math,english}/gradeX/

Assessments (one per subject per grade): materials/assessments/{math,english}/gradeX/AS-<SUBJ><grade>.md (+ _key.md)

Logs: project_logs/conversations/misc/YYYY-MM-DD/

Template: curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/_TEMPLATE_SECONDARY_MAP.md

Validator script: ./tools/validate_stage5.sh

1) File Naming & Codes (stay consistent)

Course map names: MTH1W.md, ENL1W.md, MHF4U.md, MCV4U.md, MDM4U.md, etc.

Worksheet IDs: WS-M9-001, WS-E11-007, WS-M12-014 (prefix: WS-<SubjectLetter or M/E + grade>-###).

Assessment IDs: AS-M9, AS-E11, AS-M12 (one per subject per grade).

Expectation codes: A1, C2.4, B3.1 (match the PDF exactly).

2) Map Structure (must-have sections)

Frontmatter (course, grade, subject, stream, stage, source_pdf: path)

1) Strands Overview (names only)

2) Overall Expectations (verbatim; grouped by strand)

3) Specific Expectations (verbatim with codes; grouped by strand)

4) Planning Tables

4.1 Worksheet Plan (rows by expectation code)

4.2 Assessment Plan (one table; then strand coverage)

5) Changelog (dated lines)

3) One-Shot Scaffold (new course)

Use when starting a new course map (copy, open, replace, commit, push).git add curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/ENL3W.md
git commit -m "docs(ENL3W): add Overall Expectations A‚ÄìD (verbatim)"
git pushgit add curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/MHF4U.md
git commit -m "docs(MHF4U): add Specific Expectations Strands A‚ÄìE (verbatim)"
git push 5) Planning Tables: quick patterns to paste
Worksheet Plan row (example).   | C1.2 | Drafting & revising | WS-E11-008 | vA‚ÄìvD | process writing |.  Assessment Plan block (example).  | AS-M12 | Math | 12 | 1 | Strands A‚ÄìE | Placement diagnostic |.  Strand Coverage rows should list sample expectation codes per strand (e.g., C1.1, C1.2, C2.1, C3.1), purely as a coverage cue, not a promise of 1-to-1 questions.     # For zsh (macOS default):
cat >> ~/.zshrc <<'EOF'
backupchat() {
  DATE=$(date +%Y-%m-%d)
  DIR="project_logs/conversations/misc/$DATE"
  mkdir -p "$DIR"
  FILE="$DIR/${DATE}_chat_full.md"
  echo "üëâ COPY the entire chat now (‚åòA, ‚åòC). When ready, press ENTER here‚Ä¶"
  read
  pbpaste > "$FILE"
  # Optional split: first 2000 lines as part01
  head -n 2000 "$FILE" > "$DIR/${DATE}_chat_part01.md"
  git add "$DIR"/*
  git commit -m "backup: [misc] chat split into parts for $DATE"
  git push || { git pull --rebase --autostash && git push; }
}
EOF
source ~/.zshrc
6) ‚ÄúBackup Chat‚Äù (Terminal helper)

If the backup alias disappears, re-add it:    Usage:backupchat
# (Paste with ‚åòV into the terminal prompt when it asks? No‚Äîjust press Enter.
# The function grabs your clipboard with pbpaste.).    7) Validator (run often) ./tools/validate_stage5.sh || true.  Sections OK ‚Üí your map is structurally valid.

It also lists found expectation codes (quick sanity check).

If placeholders or archives show warnings, keep them under _archive/.

8) Git Quick-Fix Cheats

‚Äúfetch first / failed to push some refs‚Äù.  git fetch origin
git pull --rebase origin main
git push.   git fetch origin
git push --force-with-lease origin main.  Stage before commit.    git add -A
git commit -m "wip: save".  printf "%s\n" "README.md.bak" >> .gitignore
git add .gitignore
git commit -m "chore: ignore local backup files"
git push.    9) Quality Checklist (tick every time)

 Frontmatter filled + source_pdf: path correct.

 Strands Overview present.

 Overall expectations: verbatim, all strands present.

 Specific expectations: verbatim with correct codes and order.

 Worksheet Plan rows cover each specific expectation (or explicitly ‚ÄúTBD‚Äù).

 Assessment Plan present with one assessment for the grade/subject + strand coverage.

 Changelog updated (date + short description).

 Validator passes (Sections OK).

 Commit messages scoped (docs(ENL3W): ‚Ä¶, feat(AS-M9): ‚Ä¶, chore: ‚Ä¶).

demonstrate an understanding of rate of change by making connections between average rate of change over an interval and instantaneous rate of change at a point, using the slopes of secants and tangents and the concept of the limit;

graph the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of a function and its derivative;

verify graphically and algebraically the rules for determining derivatives; apply these rules to determine the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, exponential, rational, and radical functions, and simple combinations of functions; and solve related problems. 
edu.gov.on.ca

Strand B ‚Äî Derivatives and Their Applications
make connections, graphically and algebraically, between the key features of a function and its first and second derivatives, and use the connections in curve sketching;

solve problems, including optimization problems, that require the use of the concepts and procedures associated with the derivative, including problems arising from real-world applications and involving the development of mathematical models. 
edu.gov.on.ca

Strand C ‚Äî Geometry and Algebra of Vectors
demonstrate an understanding of vectors in two-space and three-space by representing them algebraically and geometrically and by recognizing their applications;

perform operations on vectors in two-space and three-space, and use the properties of these operations to solve problems, including those arising from real-world applications;

distinguish between the geometric representations of a single linear equation or a system of two linear equations in two-space and three-space, and determine different geometric configurations of lines and planes in three-space;

represent lines and planes using scalar, vector, and parametric equations, and solve problems involving distances and intersections. 
edu.gov.on.ca

MCV4U ‚Äî Specific Expectations (Strand A) to paste now
Put these under ## 3) Specific Expectations ‚Üí ### Strand A.

1. Investigating Instantaneous Rate of Change at a Point
By the end of this course, students will:
1.1 describe examples of real-world applications of rates of change, represented in a variety of ways (e.g., in words, numerically, graphically, algebraically)
1.2 describe connections between the average rate of change of a function that is smooth (i.e., continuous with no corners) over an interval and the slope of the corresponding secant, and between the instantaneous rate of change of a smooth function at a point and the slope of the tangent at that point
1.3 make connections, with or without graphing technology, between an approximate value of the instantaneous rate of change at a given point on the graph of a smooth function and average rates of change over intervals containing the point (i.e., by using secants through the given point on a smooth curve to approach the tangent at that point, and determining the slopes of the approaching secants to approximate the slope of the tangent)
1.4 recognize, through investigation with or without technology, graphical and numerical examples of limits, and explain the reasoning involved (e.g., the value of a function approaching an asymptote, the value of the ratio of successive terms in the Fibonacci sequence)
1.5 make connections, for a function that is smooth over the interval

üìÑ MCV4U ‚Äî Overall Expectations (verbatim, scaffolded)
## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Rate of Change
By the end of this course, students will:  
- demonstrate an understanding of rate of change by making connections between average rate of change over an interval and instantaneous rate of change at a point, using the slopes of secants and tangents and the concept of the limit;  
- graph the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of a function and its derivative;  
- verify graphically and algebraically the rules for determining derivatives; apply these rules to determine the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, exponential, rational, and radical functions, and simple combinations of functions; and solve related problems.  

### Strand B ‚Äî Derivatives and Their Applications
By the end of this course, students will:  
- make connections, graphically and algebraically, between the key features of a function and its first and second derivatives, and use the connections in curve sketching;  
- solve problems, including optimization problems, that require the use of the concepts and procedures associated with the derivative, including problems arising from real-world applications and involving the development of mathematical models.  

### Strand C ‚Äî Geometry and Algebra of Vectors
By the end of this course, students will:  
- demonstrate an understanding of vectors in two-space and three-space by representing them algebraically and geometrically and by recognizing their applications;  
- perform operations on vectors in two-space and three-space, and use the properties of these operations to solve problems, including those arising from real-world applications;  
- distinguish between the geometric representations of a single linear equation or a system of two linear equations in two-space and three-space, and determine different geometric configurations of lines and planes in three-space;  
- represent lines and planes using scalar, vector, and parametric equations, and solve problems involving distances and intersections.

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Rate of Change
By the end of this course, students will:  
- demonstrate an understanding of rate of change by making connections between average rate of change over an interval and instantaneous rate of change at a point, using the slopes of secants and tangents and the concept of the limit;  
- graph the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of a function and its derivative;  
- verify graphically and algebraically the rules for determining derivatives; apply these rules to determine the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, exponential, rational, and radical functions, and simple combinations of functions; and solve related problems.  

### Strand B ‚Äî Derivatives and Their Applications
By the end of this course, students will:  
- make connections, graphically and algebraically, between the key features of a function and its first and second derivatives, and use the connections in curve sketching;  
- solve problems, including optimization problems, that require the use of the concepts and procedures associated with the derivative, including problems arising from real-world applications and involving the development of mathematical models.  

### Strand C ‚Äî Geometry and Algebra of Vectors
By the end of this course, students will:  
- demonstrate an understanding of vectors in two-space and three-space by representing them algebraically and geometrically and by recognizing their applications;  
- perform operations on vectors in two-space and three-space, and use the properties of these operations to solve problems, including those arising from real-world applications;  
- distinguish between the geometric representations of a single linear equation or a system of two linear equations in two-space and three-space, and determine different geometric configurations of lines and planes in three-space;  
- represent lines and planes using scalar, vector, and parametric equations, and solve problems involving distances and intersections.

ChatGPT said:
Perfect ‚úÖ ‚Äî here‚Äôs the Specific Expectations for MCV4U, Strand A in scaffold-ready format. You‚Äôll paste this under ## 3) Specific Expectations ‚Üí ### Strand A.

üìÑ MCV4U ‚Äî Specific Expectations (Strand A)
### Strand A ‚Äî Rate of Change

By the end of this course, students will:

**Investigating Instantaneous Rate of Change at a Point**

- A1.1 describe examples of real-world applications of rates of change, represented in a variety of ways (e.g., in words, numerically, graphically, algebraically).  
- A1.2 describe connections between the average rate of change of a function that is smooth (i.e., continuous with no corners) over an interval and the slope of the corresponding secant, and between the instantaneous rate of change of a smooth function at a point and the slope of the tangent at that point.  
- A1.3 make connections, with or without graphing technology, between an approximate value of the instantaneous rate of change at a given point on the graph of a smooth function and average rates of change over intervals containing the point (i.e., by using secants through the given point on a smooth curve to approach the tangent at that point, and determining the slopes of the approaching secants to approximate the slope of the tangent).  
- A1.4 recognize, through investigation with or without technology, graphical and numerical examples of limits, and explain the reasoning involved (e.g., the value of a function approaching an asymptote, the value of the ratio of successive terms in the Fibonacci sequence).  
- A1.5 make connections, for a function that is smooth over the interval \(a \le x \le a + h\), between the average rate of change of the function over this interval and the value of the expression \(\frac{f(a+h)-f(a)}{h}\), and between the instantaneous rate of change of the function at \(x=a\) and the value of the limit \(\lim_{h\to 0}\frac{f(a+h)-f(a)}{h}\).

ChatGPT said:
Here is the fully redrafted scaffold for MCF3M (Grade 11 Functions & Applications), incorporating the exact information for the Overall Expectations (strands A, B, C) directly from the official Ontario curriculum:

MCF3M ‚Äî Functions and Applications (Grade 11)
# MCF3M ‚Äî Functions and Applications

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Quadratic Functions
- B. Exponential Functions
- C. Trigonometric Functions

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- Expand and simplify quadratic expressions, solve quadratic equations, and relate the roots of a quadratic equation to the corresponding graph;
- Demonstrate an understanding of functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of quadratic functions;
- Solve problems involving quadratic functions, including problems arising from real-world applications. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

### Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- Simplify and evaluate numerical expressions involving exponents, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of exponential functions;
- Identify and represent exponential functions, and solve problems involving exponential functions, including problems arising from real-world applications;
- Demonstrate an understanding of compound interest and annuities, and solve related problems. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

### Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- Solve problems involving trigonometry in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law, including problems arising from real-world applications;
- Demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and the sine function, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of sine functions;
- Identify and represent sine functions, and solve problems involving sine functions, including problems arising from real-world applications. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

MCF3M ‚Äî Functions and Applications (Grade 11)
# MCF3M ‚Äî Functions and Applications

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Quadratic Functions  
- B. Exponential Functions  
- C. Trigonometric Functions  

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions  
By the end of this course, students will:  
- Expand and simplify quadratic expressions, solve quadratic equations, and relate the roots of a quadratic equation to the corresponding graph;  
- Demonstrate an understanding of functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of quadratic functions;  
- Solve problems involving quadratic functions, including problems arising from real-world applications. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}  

### Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions  
By the end of this course, students will:  
- Simplify and evaluate numerical expressions involving exponents, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of exponential functions;  
- Identify and represent exponential functions, and solve problems involving exponential functions, including problems arising from real-world applications;  
- Demonstrate an understanding of compound interest and annuities, and solve related problems. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}  

### Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions  
By the end of this course, students will:  
- Solve problems involving trigonometry in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law, including problems arising from real-world applications;  
- Demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and the sine function, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of sine functions;  
- Identify and represent sine functions, and solve problems involving sine functions, including problems arising from real-world applications. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Absolutely! Here's the Specific Expectations for MCF3M (Functions & Applications, Grade 11), fully formatted and ready for you to paste into your scaffold. I'll provide each strand one after the other so they're easy to drop in.

MCF3M ‚Äî Specific Expectations (Strand A)
### Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions

By the end of the course, students will:

- A1.1 Expand and simplify quadratic expressions, solve quadratic equations, and relate the roots of a quadratic equation to the corresponding graph.  
- A1.2 Demonstrate an understanding of functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of quadratic functions.  
- A1.3 Solve problems involving quadratic functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.  
MCF3M ‚Äî Specific Expectations (Strand B)
### Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions

By the end of the course, students will:

- B1.1 Simplify and evaluate numerical expressions involving exponents, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of exponential functions.  
- B1.2 Identify and represent exponential functions, and solve problems involving exponential functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.  
- B1.3 Demonstrate an understanding of compound interest and annuities, and solve related problems.  
MCF3M ‚Äî Specific Expectations (Strand C)
### Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions

By the end of the course, students will:

- C1.1 Solve problems involving trigonometry in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law, including problems arising from real-world applications.  
- C1.2 Demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and the sine function, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of sine functions.  
- C1.3 Identify and represent sine functions, and solve problems involving sine functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.

Got it ‚úÖ ‚Äî let‚Äôs focus on MCF3M (Functions and Applications, Grade 11) and pull together a detailed course map so your MCF3M.md is accurate, complete, and scaffolded correctly.

üìò MCF3M ‚Äî Functions and Applications (Ontario Curriculum)
1) Strands Overview
The course is organized into three main strands:

A. Quadratic Functions

B. Exponential Functions

C. Trigonometric Functions

2) Overall Expectations
Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions
By the end of this course, students will:

Expand and simplify quadratic expressions, solve quadratic equations, and relate the roots of a quadratic equation to the corresponding graph.

Demonstrate an understanding of functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of quadratic functions.

Solve problems involving quadratic functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.

Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions
By the end of this course, students will:

Simplify and evaluate numerical expressions involving exponents, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of exponential functions.

Identify and represent exponential functions, and solve problems involving exponential functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.

Demonstrate an understanding of compound interest and annuities, and solve related problems.

Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
By the end of this course, students will:

Solve problems involving trigonometry in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law, including problems arising from real-world applications.

Demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and the sine function, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of sine functions.

Identify and represent sine functions, and solve problems involving sine functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.

3) Specific Expectations
Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions
A1.1 Expand and simplify quadratic expressions.

A1.2 Solve quadratic equations by factoring, completing the square, and using the quadratic formula.

A1.3 Make connections between the roots of a quadratic equation and the x-intercepts of its graph.

A1.4 Demonstrate an understanding of transformations of quadratic functions.

A1.5 Solve application problems involving quadratic functions (e.g., projectile motion, optimization).

Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions
B1.1 Apply the laws of exponents to simplify and evaluate numerical expressions.

B1.2 Recognize, represent, and interpret exponential functions in various contexts.

B1.3 Solve problems involving exponential growth and decay.

B1.4 Solve problems involving compound interest, annuities, and financial applications.

Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
C1.1 Solve problems in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law.

C1.2 Demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and describe their key features.

C1.3 Graph sine functions and make connections among numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations.

C1.4 Solve real-world problems involving sine functions (e.g., tides, seasonal changes).

4) Planning Tables
4.1 Worksheet Plan
Expectation Code	Topic / Focus	Worksheet ID	Versions	Notes
A1.1	Expanding & simplifying quadratics	WS-M11-001	vA‚ÄìvD	
A1.2	Solving quadratic equations	WS-M11-002	vA‚ÄìvD

A1.4	Transformations of quadratics	WS-M11-004	vA‚ÄìvD	
A1.5	Quadratic applications	WS-M11-005	vA‚ÄìvD	
B1.1	Exponent laws	WS-M11-006	vA‚ÄìvD	
B1.2	Exponential functions basics	WS-M11-007	vA‚ÄìvD	
B1.3	Growth & decay problems	WS-M11-008	vA‚ÄìvD	
B1.4	Compound interest & annuities	WS-M11-009	vA‚ÄìvD	
C1.1	Sine & cosine law	WS-M11-010	vA‚ÄìvD	
C1.2	Periodic relationships	WS-M11-011	vA‚ÄìvD

# MCF3M ‚Äî Functions and Applications

stage: 6
grade: 11
subject: Mathematics
course_code: MCF3M
stream: University/College Preparation
source_pdf: curriculum/ontario/secondary/math/MCF3M.pdf

---

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Quadratic Functions
- B. Exponential Functions
- C. Trigonometric Functions

---

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions
By the end of this course, students will:  
- expand and simplify quadratic expressions, solve quadratic equations, and relate the roots of a quadratic equation to the corresponding graph;  
- demonstrate an understanding of functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of quadratic functions;  
- solve problems involving quadratic functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.  

### Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions
By the end of this course, students will:  
- simplify and evaluate numerical expressions involving exponents, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of exponential functions;  
- identify and represent exponential functions, and solve problems involving exponential functions, including problems arising from real-world applications;  
- demonstrate an understanding of compound interest and annuities, and solve related problems.  

### Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
By the end of this course, students will:  
- solve problems involving trigonometry in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law, including problems arising from real-world applications;  
- demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and the sine function, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of sine functions;  
- identify and represent sine functions, and solve problems involving sine functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.  

---

## 3) Specific Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions
- A1.1 Expand and simplify quadratic expressions.  
- A1.2 Solve quadratic equations by factoring, completing the square, and using the quadratic formula.  
- A1.3 Make connections between the roots of a quadratic equation and the x-intercepts of its graph.  
- A1.4 Demonstrate an understanding of transformations of quadratic functions.  
- A1.5 Solve application problems involving quadratic functions (e.g., projectile motion, optimization).  

### Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions
- B1.1 Apply the laws of exponents to simplify and evaluate numerical expressions.  
- B1.2 Recognize, represent, and interpret exponential functions in various contexts.  
- B1.3 Solve problems involving exponential growth and decay.  
- B1.4 Solve problems involving compound interest, annuities, and financial applications.  

### Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
- C1.1 Solve problems in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law.  
- C1.2 Demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and describe their key features.  
- C1.3 Graph sine functions and make connections among numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations.  
- C1.4 Solve real-world problems involving sine functions (e.g., tides, seasonal changes).  

---

## 4) Planning Tables

### 4.1 Worksheet Plan
| Expectation Code | Topic / Focus                  | Worksheet ID | Versions | Notes |
|------------------|--------------------------------|--------------|----------|-------|
| A1.1             | Expanding & simplifying quadratics | WS-M11-001 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| A1.2             | Solving quadratic equations        | WS-M11-002 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| A1.3             | Quadratic roots & graphs           | WS-M11-003 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| A1.4             | Transformations of quadratics      | WS-M11-004 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| A1.5             | Quadratic applications             | WS-M11-005 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| B1.1             | Exponent laws                     | WS-M11-006 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| B1.2             | Exponential functions basics       | WS-M11-007 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| B1.3             | Growth & decay problems            | WS-M11-008 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| B1.4             | Compound interest & annuities      | WS-M11-009 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| C1.1             | Sine & cosine law                  | WS-M11-010 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| C1.2             | Periodic relationships             | WS-M11-011 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| C1.3             | Graphing sine functions            | WS-M11-012 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |
| C1.4             | Applications of sine functions     | WS-M11-013 | vA‚ÄìvD   |       |

| Assessment ID | Subject | Grade | Count | Strand Coverage | Notes                          |
|---------------|---------|-------|-------|-----------------|--------------------------------|

**Strand Coverage**  
- Strand A: A1.1‚ÄìA1.5  
- Strand B: B1.1‚ÄìB1.4  
- Strand C: C1.1‚ÄìC1.4

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 12s
Awesome‚Äîlet‚Äôs do a quick QA sweep across all secondary course maps to catch any missing sections, placeholders, or mapping gaps. Below is a single, paste-ready shell block that generates a human-readable report and points to fixes.

üîé Stage 6 ‚Äî Secondary Maps QA Sweep (one-shot)
# From repo root
set -euo pipefail

OUTDIR="project_logs/conversations/misc/$(date +%F)"
OUTFILE="$OUTDIR/secondary_maps_QA_report.txt"
mkdir -p "$OUTDIR"

echo "RuberuTutor ‚Äî Secondary Maps QA Report  ($(date))" > "$OUTFILE"
echo "Repo: $(pwd)" >> "$OUTFILE"
echo "======================================================================" >> "$OUTFILE"

# Collect all secondary maps except the template and archived items
MAPS=$(ls curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/*.md \
  | grep -v '_TEMPLATE_SECONDARY_MAP.md' \
  | grep -v '/_archive/')

# Helper: print a header per file
ph() { printf "\n\n## %s\n" "$1" >> "$OUTFILE"; }

# Regexes
SEC_RE='^## [0-9]\) (Strands Overview|Overall Expectations|Specific Expectations|Planning Tables)$'
PLACEHOLDERS='(\[verbatim\]|\[from PDF\]|\[title\]|TBD|‚Ä¶|^\s*-\s*\[TBD\]|^\s*-\s*\[verbatim\])'
EXP_CODE_RE='[A-Z][0-9]+(\.[0-9]+)?'  # e.g., A1, B2.1

for f in $MAPS; do
  ph "$f"

  echo "- Basic metadata/frontmatter check:" >> "$OUTFILE"
  (grep -E '^(course|course:|course_code:|grade:|subject:|stream:|stage:|source_pdf:)' -n "$f" \
    || true) | sed 's/^/    /' >> "$OUTFILE"

  echo "- Required sections present:" >> "$OUTFILE"
  for sec in "## 1) Strands Overview" "## 2) Overall Expectations" "## 3) Specific Expectations" "## 4) Planning Tables"; do
    if grep -qF "$sec" "$f"; then
      echo "    ‚úì $sec" >> "$OUTFILE"
    else
      echo "    ‚úó MISSING: $sec" >> "$OUTFILE"
    fi
  done

  echo "- Placeholder scan (should be ZERO hits):" >> "$OUTFILE"
  PH=$(grep -En "$PLACEHOLDERS" "$f" || true)
  if [ -z "$PH" ]; then
    echo "    ‚úì No placeholders found" >> "$OUTFILE"
  else
    echo "$PH" | sed 's/^/    ‚ö† /' >> "$OUTFILE"
  fi

  echo "- Expectation code scan (format like A1, B2.1, etc.):" >> "$OUTFILE"
  (grep -En "$EXP_CODE_RE" "$f" || true) | sed 's/^/    ‚Ä¢ /' >> "$OUTFILE"

  echo "- Worksheet Plan rows (quick count):" >> "$OUTFILE"
  if awk '/^### 4\.1 Worksheet Plan/{flag=1;next}/^### 4\.2 Assessment Plan/{flag=0}flag' "$f" \
      | grep -E '^\| *[A-Z][0-9]+(\.[0-9]+)? *\|' >/dev/null 2>&1; then
    COUNT=$(awk '/^### 4\.1 Worksheet Plan/{flag=1;next}/^### 4\.2 Assessment Plan/{flag=0}flag' "$f" \
      | grep -E '^\| *[A-Z][0-9]+(\.[0-9]+)? *\|' | wc -l | tr -d ' ')
    echo "    ‚úì Rows found: $COUNT" >> "$OUTFILE"
  else
    echo "    ‚úó No worksheet rows detected between 4.1 and 4.2" >> "$OUTFILE"
  fi

  echo "- Assessment Plan sanity:" >> "$OUTFILE"
  if grep -q '^### 4\.2 Assessment Plan' "$f"; then
    if grep -E '^\| *AS-[A-Z0-9]+' "$f" >/dev/null; then
      echo "    ‚úì Assessment ID present" >> "$OUTFILE"
    else
      echo "    ‚ö† Assessment table present but no AS-* ID detected" >> "$OUTFILE"
    fi
  else
    echo "    ‚úó Missing 4.2 Assessment Plan section" >> "$OUTFILE"
  fi
done

echo -e "\n======================================================================" >> "$OUTFILE"
echo "Validator output:" >> "$OUTFILE"
./tools/validate_stage5.sh || true >> "$OUTFILE" 2>&1

echo -e "\n‚úÖ Done. See report:\n$OUTFILE"
What this does

Checks frontmatter fields exist.

Verifies required sections (1‚Äì4) are present.

Flags placeholders ([verbatim], [from PDF], TBD, ‚Ä¶, [title]), which should be cleared for finished maps.

Lists all expectation codes it finds (quick scan).

Counts Worksheet Plan rows between 4.1 and 4.2.

Sanity-checks the Assessment Plan for an AS-* ID.

Appends your validator output to the same report for side-by-side review.

# MCF3M ‚Äî Functions and Applications

stage: 6
grade: 11
subject: Mathematics
course_code: MCF3M
stream: University/College Preparation
source_pdf: curriculum/ontario/secondary/math/MCF3M.pdf

---

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Quadratic Functions
- B. Exponential Functions
- C. Trigonometric Functions

---

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- expand and simplify quadratic expressions, solve quadratic equations, and relate the roots of a quadratic equation to the corresponding graph;
- demonstrate an understanding of functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of quadratic functions;
- solve problems involving quadratic functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.

### Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- simplify and evaluate numerical expressions involving exponents, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of exponential functions;
- identify and represent exponential functions, and solve problems involving exponential functions, including problems arising from real-world applications;
- demonstrate an understanding of compound interest and annuities, and solve related problems.

### Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- solve problems involving trigonometry in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law, including problems arising from real-world applications;
- demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and the sine function, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of sine functions;
- identify and represent sine functions, and solve problems involving sine functions, including problems arising from real-world applications.

---

## 3) Specific Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Quadratic Functions
- A1.1 Expand and simplify quadratic expressions.
- A1.2 Solve quadratic equations by factoring, completing the square, and using the quadratic formula.
- A1.3 Make connections between the roots of a quadratic equation and the x-intercepts of its graph.
- A1.4 Demonstrate an understanding of transformations of quadratic functions.
- A1.5 Solve application problems involving quadratic functions (e.g., projectile motion, optimization).

### Strand B ‚Äî Exponential Functions
- B1.1 Apply the laws of exponents to simplify and evaluate numerical expressions.
- B1.2 Recognize, represent, and interpret exponential functions in various contexts.
- B1.3 Solve problems involving exponential growth and decay.
- B1.4 Solve problems involving compound interest, annuities, and financial applications.

### Strand C ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
- C1.1 Solve problems in acute triangles using the sine law and the cosine law.
- C1.2 Demonstrate an understanding of periodic relationships and describe their key features.
- C1.3 Graph sine functions and make connections among numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations.
- C1.4 Solve real-world problems involving sine functions (e.g., tides, seasonal changes).

---

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 36s
You‚Äôve got a bad line in ~/.zshrc: there‚Äôs an alias named backupchat and then you try to define a function with the same name, which makes zsh choke (parse error near '()'). Let‚Äôs fix it cleanly.

Quick fix (safe + copy-paste)
# 0) Backup your zshrc
cp ~/.zshrc ~/.zshrc.bak.$(date +%F_%H%M%S)

# 1) Remove any alias line for backupchat
# (macOS sed needs the empty string after -i)
sed -i '' '/^alias[[:space:]]\+backupchat=/d' ~/.zshrc

# 2) Append a guarded function definition
cat >> ~/.zshrc <<'EOF'
# --- RuberuTutor helper: backupchat ---
unalias backupchat 2>/dev/null

backupchat() {
  local DATE
  DATE=$(date +%Y-%m-%d)
  local DIR="$HOME/ruberututor-curriculum/project_logs/conversations/misc/$DATE"
  mkdir -p "$DIR"
  local FILE="$DIR/${DATE}_chat_full.md"
  echo "üëâ COPY the entire chat now (‚åòA, ‚åòC). When ready, press ENTER here‚Ä¶"
  read
  pbpaste > "$FILE"
  # Optional split: first 2000 lines as part01 (ignore errors if shorter)
  head -n 2000 "$FILE" > "$DIR/${DATE}_chat_part01.md" 2>/dev/null || true
  # Commit to the repo
  cd "$HOME/ruberututor-curriculum" || return
  git add "$DIR"/*
  git commit -m "backup: [misc] chat split into parts for $DATE"
  git push || { git pull --rebase --autostash && git push; }
}
# --- end helper ---
EOF

# 3) Reload your shell config
source ~/.zshrc

# 4) Sanity-check the function exists
type backupchat
You should now see something like: backupchat is a shell function.

(Optional) Re-run your repo checks
cd ~/ruberututor-curriculum
git status
./tools/validate_stage5.sh || true
If anything else in .zshrc still errors, open it and look for stray quotes/backticks:

nano ~/.zshrc
# tip: in nano press Ctrl+W, type backupchat to jump to the function block

backupchat() {
  local DATE DIR FILE

  pbpaste > "$FILE"

}

# MHF4U ‚Äî Advanced Functions

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Exponential and Logarithmic Functions
- B. Trigonometric Functions
- C. Polynomial and Rational Functions
- D. Characteristics of Functions

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Exponential and Logarithmic Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of the relationship between exponential expressions and logarithmic expressions; evaluate logarithms and apply the laws of logarithms to simplify numeric expressions;
- identify and describe key features of logarithmic function graphs; connect numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations and solve related problems graphically;
- solve exponential and simple logarithmic equations in one variable algebraically, including real-world application problems.

### Strand B ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of radian measure and its application;
- connect trigonometric ratios with graphical and algebraic representations of trigonometric functions and their reciprocals; use these connections to solve problems;
- solve trigonometric equations and prove trigonometric identities.

### Strand C ‚Äî Polynomial and Rational Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- identify and describe key features of polynomial functions and connect their numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations;
- identify and describe key features of rational function graphs and represent rational functions graphically;
- solve polynomial and simple rational equations both graphically and algebraically;
- demonstrate an understanding of solving polynomial and simple rational inequalities.

### Strand D ‚Äî Characteristics of Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- understand average and instantaneous rate of change and interpret them numerically and graphically over given intervals;
- form functions resulting from operations (addition, subtraction, multiplication, division, composition), describe properties, and solve related problems;
- compare characteristics of functions using modeling and reasoning, including problems not easily solvable algebraically.

Here's your fully scaffolded MHF4U.md with both Overall Expectations and Specific Expectations filled in verbatim from the Ministry of Education. Ready to paste into your curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary/MHF4U.md:

---
course: MHF4U

# MHF4U ‚Äî Advanced Functions

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Exponential and Logarithmic Functions  
- B. Trigonometric Functions  
- C. Polynomial and Rational Functions  
- D. Characteristics of Functions  

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Exponential and Logarithmic Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of the relationship between exponential expressions and logarithmic expressions; evaluate logarithms, and apply the laws of logarithms to simplify numeric expressions;
- identify and describe some key features of the graphs of logarithmic functions, make connections among the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of logarithmic functions, and solve related problems graphically;
- solve exponential and simple logarithmic equations in one variable algebraically, including those in problems arising from real-world applications. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

### Strand B ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of the meaning and application of radian measure;
- make connections between trigonometric ratios and the graphical and algebraic representations of the corresponding trigonometric functions and between trigonometric functions and their reciprocals, and use these connections to solve problems;
- solve problems involving trigonometric equations and prove trigonometric identities. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

### Strand C ‚Äî Polynomial and Rational Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- identify and describe some key features of polynomial functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of polynomial functions;
- identify and describe some key features of the graphs of rational functions, and represent rational functions graphically;
- solve problems involving polynomial and simple rational equations graphically and algebraically;
- demonstrate an understanding of solving polynomial and simple rational inequalities. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

### Strand D ‚Äî Characteristics of Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of average and instantaneous rate of change, and determine, numerically and graphically, and interpret the average rate of change of a function over a given interval and the instantaneous rate of change of a function at a given point;
- determine functions that result from the addition, subtraction, multiplication, and division of two functions and from the composition of two functions, describe some properties of the resulting functions, and solve related problems;
- compare the characteristics of functions, and solve problems by modeling and reasoning with functions, including problems with solutions that are not accessible by standard algebraic techniques. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

## 3) Specific Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Exponential and Logarithmic Functions
- A1.1 demonstrate an understanding of the relationship between exponential expressions and logarithmic expressions;
- A1.2 evaluate logarithms; 
- A1.3 apply the laws of logarithms to simplify numeric expressions;
- A1.4 identify and describe key features of graphs of logarithmic functions;
- A1.5 connect numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of logarithmic functions;
- A1.6 solve exponential and simple logarithmic equations in one variable, including real-world applications.

### Strand B ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
- B1.1 demonstrate an understanding of the meaning and application of radian measure;
- B1.2 connect trigonometric ratios with graphical and algebraic representations of trigonometric functions and their reciprocals;
- B1.3 use these connections to solve problems;
- B1.4 solve problems involving trigonometric equations;
- B1.5 prove trigonometric identities.

### Strand C ‚Äî Polynomial and Rational Functions
- C1.1 identify and describe key features of polynomial functions, connecting numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations;
- C1.2 identify and describe features of rational function graphs and represent them graphically;
- C1.3 solve polynomial and simple rational equations graphically and algebraically;
- C1.4 demonstrate understanding of solving polynomial and simple rational inequalities.

### Strand D ‚Äî Characteristics of Functions
- D1.1 demonstrate an understanding of average and instantaneous rate of change, interpreting numerically and graphically;
- D1.2 determine properties of functions resulting from addition, subtraction, multiplication, division, and composition of functions, and solve related problems;
- D1.3 compare characteristics of functions modelled in reasoning, including problems not solvable algebraically.

## 4) Planning Tables

### 4.1 Worksheet Plan
| Expectation Code | Topic / Focus                     | Worksheet ID | Versions | Notes |
|------------------|-----------------------------------|--------------|----------|-------|
| A1.1‚ÄìA1.3        | Exponential & logarithmic basics  | WS-M12-001   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| A1.4‚ÄìA1.5        | Graphing & representations        | WS-M12-002   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| A1.6             | Equation solving applications     | WS-M12-003   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| B1.1             | Radian measure                    | WS-M12-004   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| B1.2‚ÄìB1.3        | Trig representations & problem-solving | WS-M12-005 | vA‚ÄìvD  |       |
| B1.4‚ÄìB1.5        | Equations & identities            | WS-M12-006   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| C1.1             | Polynomial functions              | WS-M12-007   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| C1.2             | Rational function features        | WS-M12-008   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| C1.3             | Equation solving‚Äîpolynomial/rational | WS-M12-009 | vA‚ÄìvD |       |
| C1.4             | Inequalities                      | WS-M12-010   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| D1.1             | Rates of change                   | WS-M12-011   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| D1.2‚ÄìD1.3        | Combining & modeling functions    | WS-M12-012   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |

### 4.2 Assessment Plan
| Assessment ID | Subject | Grade | Count | Strand Coverage | Notes                          |
|---------------|---------|-------|-------|-----------------|--------------------------------|
| **AS-M12A**   | Math    | 12    | 1     | Strands A‚ÄìD     | Culminating; covers all strands |

**Strand Coverage**  
- A: A1.1‚ÄìA1.6  
- B: B1.1‚ÄìB1.5

# MCV4U ‚Äî Calculus and Vectors

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Rate of Change
- B. Derivatives and Their Applications
- C. Geometry and Algebra of Vectors

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Rate of Change
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of rate of change by making connections between average rate of change over an interval, instantaneous rate of change, and the slope of a tangent to a curve;
- graph the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions, and make connections between the numeric, graphical, and algebraic representations of a function and its derivative;
- verify graphically and algebraically the rules for determining derivatives; apply these rules to determine the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions; and solve related problems.

### Strand B ‚Äî Derivatives and Their Applications
By the end of this course, students will:
- make connections, graphically and algebraically, between the key features of a function and its first and second derivatives and use these connections to solve problems;
- solve problems, including optimization problems, that require the use of the concepts and procedures associated with the derivative, including problems arising from real-world applications.

### Strand C ‚Äî Geometry and Algebra of Vectors
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of vectors in two-space and three-space by representing them algebraically and geometrically and by recognizing their applications;
- perform operations on vectors in two-space and three-space, and use the properties of these operations to solve problems, including those arising from real-world applications;
- distinguish between the geometric representations of a single linear equation or a system of two linear equations in two-space, and of a single linear equation or a system of two linear equations in three-space;
- represent lines and planes using scalar, vector, and parametric equations, and solve problems involving distances and intersections.

üìò MCV4U ‚Äî Specific Expectations (Full Draft)
## 3) Specific Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Rate of Change
By the end of this course, students will:

- **A1.1** distinguish between average rate of change over an interval and instantaneous rate of change at a point, using numerical and graphical representations, and apply these concepts in real-world contexts;
- **A1.2** estimate instantaneous rate of change of a function at a point, given the graph of the function, and verify using the slopes of secants;
- **A1.3** make connections, numerically, graphically, and algebraically, between a function and its first derivative, and describe these connections;
- **A1.4** determine the derivatives of polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions, using the product rule, quotient rule, chain rule, and rules for derivatives of basic functions, and verify using numeric and graphical representations;
- **A1.5** solve problems involving average and instantaneous rates of change in applications drawn from the natural and social sciences.

---

### Strand B ‚Äî Derivatives and Their Applications
By the end of this course, students will:

- **B1.1** make connections between the sign of the first derivative of a function and the intervals over which the function is increasing or decreasing, and use these connections to sketch graphs of polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions;
- **B1.2** make connections between the sign of the second derivative of a function and the concavity of the function, and between points of inflection and changes in concavity, and use these connections to sketch graphs of polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions;
- **B1.3** sketch the graph of a polynomial, sinusoidal, or exponential function, given information concerning the function and its first and second derivatives;
- **B1.4** solve optimization problems involving polynomial, sinusoidal, and exponential functions, and interpret the solutions in the context of the problems;
- **B1.5** solve problems, including those arising from real-world applications, involving rates of change, by applying differentiation techniques.

---

### Strand C ‚Äî Geometry and Algebra of Vectors
By the end of this course, students will:

- **C1.1** represent vectors in two-space and three-space algebraically and geometrically, and compute their magnitudes;
- **C1.2** perform addition, subtraction, and scalar multiplication of vectors, and interpret these operations geometrically and algebraically;
- **C1.3** determine the dot product of two vectors, and use it to solve problems, including those arising from applications;
- **C2.1** distinguish between a direction vector and a position vector, and between a scalar equation and vector equation of a line, and use these to represent lines in two-space and three-space;
- **C2.2** determine parametric equations of lines and planes, and use them to solve problems;
- **C2.3** determine the equation of a plane, given a point on the plane and a normal vector, and solve problems involving distances between points, lines, and planes;
- **C3.1** determine, through investigation, the conditions under which systems of two linear equations in three variables have no solution, a unique solution, or infinitely many solutions, and solve related problems;
- **C3.2** solve problems involving intersections of lines and planes, and distances between points, lines, and planes.

---

üìò MHF4U ‚Äî Advanced Functions (Full Draft in Scaffold Format)
# MHF4U ‚Äî Advanced Functions

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Characteristics of Functions
- B. Properties of Functions
- C. Exponential and Logarithmic Functions
- D. Trigonometric Functions
- E. Polynomial and Rational Functions

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Characteristics of Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of functions, their representations, and their inverses, and make connections between the representations;
- determine the zeros and the maximum and minimum values of polynomial functions, and solve related problems;
- demonstrate an understanding of key features of the graphs of rational functions, and represent rational functions graphically;
- determine the values of trigonometric ratios for angles less than 360¬∞, and solve related problems.

### Strand B ‚Äî Properties of Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of the equivalence of algebraic expressions involving radical and rational exponents;
- simplify expressions containing exponents and evaluate numerical expressions involving exponents and radicals;
- solve exponential equations algebraically, and solve problems involving exponential models;
- demonstrate an understanding of logarithms and their properties, and solve related problems.

### Strand C ‚Äî Exponential and Logarithmic Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- evaluate logarithmic expressions and apply the laws of logarithms to simplify expressions;
- graph exponential and logarithmic functions, and describe key features of the graphs;
- solve problems using exponential and logarithmic functions, including real-world applications.

### Strand D ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of the relationship between the unit circle and trigonometric functions;
- graph trigonometric functions and describe key features of the graphs;
- solve problems involving trigonometric equations and identities.

### Strand E ‚Äî Polynomial and Rational Functions
By the end of this course, students will:
- determine the zeros and the maximum and minimum values of polynomial functions, and solve related problems;
- graph polynomial and rational functions, and describe key features of the graphs;
- solve problems involving polynomial and rational functions, including applications.

---

## 3) Specific Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Characteristics of Functions
- **A1.1** demonstrate an understanding of function notation and the concepts of domain and range, and apply these concepts in problem-solving contexts;
- **A1.2** interpret the meaning of a function in terms of its graph and the situation it models;
- **A1.3** determine whether a relation is a function, and justify the conclusion;
- **A1.4** determine the values of a function for given values of the independent variable;
- **A1.5** determine the inverse of a function, and make connections between the function and its inverse.

### Strand B ‚Äî Properties of Functions
- **B1.1** demonstrate an understanding of the equivalence between expressions involving radicals and expressions involving rational exponents;
- **B1.2** simplify expressions involving rational exponents and radicals, and evaluate numerical expressions;
- **B1.3** solve equations involving exponential functions algebraically, and verify solutions;
- **B1.4** demonstrate an understanding of the properties of logarithms, and apply these properties to simplify expressions.

### Strand C ‚Äî Exponential and Logarithmic Functions
- **C1.1** evaluate logarithmic expressions using the laws of logarithms;
- **C1.2** graph exponential and logarithmic functions, and describe their domain, range, intercepts, and asymptotes;
- **C1.3** solve problems using exponential and logarithmic functions in real-world applications.

### Strand D ‚Äî Trigonometric Functions
- **D1.1** determine the exact values of trigonometric ratios for special angles in standard position;
- **D1.2** graph trigonometric functions, and describe their amplitude, period, and phase shift;
- **D1.3** solve problems involving trigonometric equations in degree and radian measure.

### Strand E ‚Äî Polynomial and Rational Functions
- **E1.1** determine the zeros and the maximum and minimum values of polynomial functions, and solve related problems;
- **E1.2** graph polynomial and rational functions, identifying key features such as intercepts and asymptotes;
- **E1.3** solve problems involving polynomial and rational functions, including real-world applications.

---

# From repo root
expected=( MCV4U MDM4U ENL4W ENG4U MTH2W ENL2W MCF3M MBF3C ENL1W MCR3U MHF4U ENG2D MTH1W ENL3W )
base="curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary"

echo "‚úÖ Checking presence & file sizes:"
missing=()
for c in "${expected[@]}"; do
  f="$base/$c.md"
  if [[ -f "$f" ]]; then
    printf "  ‚Ä¢ %-6s %s bytes\n" "$c" "$(wc -c < "$f")"
  else
    missing+=("$c")
  fi
done

if (( ${#missing[@]} )); then
  echo ""
  echo "‚ùå Missing course maps:"
  printf "  - %s\n" "${missing[@]}"
else
  echo ""
  echo "‚úÖ All expected course maps are present."
fi

echo ""
echo "üîé Git last commits for each map:"
for c in "${expected[@]}"; do
  f="$base/$c.md"
  [[ -f "$f" ]] && git log -1 --pretty=format:"%C(yellow)%h%Creset %ad %Cgreen(%an)%Creset %s" --date=short -- "$f"
done | sed 's/^/  ‚Ä¢ /'

You said:
how would i seperate course scaffolds from the ones that have no unique content
ChatGPT said:

Thought for 9s
Got you. Here are drop-in bash one-liners (plus an optional script) to separate ‚Äúscaffold-only‚Äù maps from maps with unique content by comparing to the template and checking for real expectation text.

Quick scan (prints two lists)
# From repo root
BASE="curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary"
TEMPLATE="$BASE/_TEMPLATE_SECONDARY_MAP.md"

echo "üîé Comparing maps against template + checking for real content‚Ä¶"

scaffold=()
filled=()

for f in "$BASE"/*.md; do
  [[ "$f" == "$TEMPLATE" ]] && continue

  # 1) Exact or near-exact match to template after stripping blank lines & trailing spaces?
  if diff -q <(sed -E 's/[[:space:]]+$//; /^[[:space:]]*$/d' "$f") \
              <(sed -E 's/[[:space:]]+$//; /^[[:space:]]*$/d' "$TEMPLATE") >/dev/null; then
    scaffold+=("$f")
    continue
  fi

  # 2) Heuristic: do we actually have non-placeholder Specific Expectations?
  # Count non-header, non-table, non-blank lines inside section 3) Specific Expectations
  se_lines=$(awk '
    /^##[[:space:]]*3\)/{insec=1; next}
    /^##[[:space:]]*[45]\)/{insec=0}
    insec && $0 !~ /^#/ && $0 !~ /^\|/ && $0 !~ /^[[:space:]]*$/ {count++}
    END{print count+0}
  ' "$f")

  # 3) Very small files (likely untouched scaffold)
  bytes=$(wc -c < "$f")

  if [[ $se_lines -lt 5 || $bytes -lt 1200 ]]; then
    scaffold+=("$f")
  else
    filled+=("$f")
  fi
done

echo ""
echo "‚úÖ Filled (unique content present):"
printf "  ‚Ä¢ %s\n" "${filled[@]}"

echo ""
echo "üß© Likely scaffold-only (no/low unique content):"
printf "  ‚Ä¢ %s\n" "${scaffold[@]}"
Save a dated report to project_logs/‚Ä¶
# From repo root
DATE=$(date +%F)
OUTDIR="project_logs/conversations/misc/$DATE"
mkdir -p "$OUTDIR"
bash -c '
BASE="curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary"
TEMPLATE="$BASE/_TEMPLATE_SECONDARY_MAP.md"
scaffold=(); filled=()
for f in "$BASE"/*.md; do
  [[ "$f" == "$TEMPLATE" ]] && continue
  if diff -q <(sed -E "s/[[:space:]]+$//; /^[[:space:]]*$/d" "$f") \
              <(sed -E "s/[[:space:]]+$//; /^[[:space:]]*$/d" "$TEMPLATE") >/dev/null; then
    scaffold+=("$f"); continue
  fi
  se_lines=$(awk '"'"'
    /^##[[:space:]]*3\)/{insec=1; next}
    /^##[[:space:]]*[45]\)/{insec=0}
    insec && $0 !~ /^#/ && $0 !~ /^\|/ && $0 !~ /^[[:space:]]*$/ {count++}
    END{print count+0}
  '"'"' "$f")
  bytes=$(wc -c < "$f")
  if [[ $se_lines -lt 5 || $bytes -lt 1200 ]]; then
    scaffold+=("$f")
  else
    filled+=("$f")
  fi
done
{
  echo "# Course Map Audit ‚Äî $DATE"
  echo ""
  echo "## Filled (unique content present)"
  for x in "${filled[@]}"; do echo "- $x ($(wc -c < "$x") bytes)"; done
  echo ""
  echo "## Likely scaffold-only"
  for x in "${scaffold[@]}"; do echo "- $x ($(wc -c < "$x") bytes)"; done
} > "'"$OUTDIR"'/course_map_audit.md"
'

git add "$OUTDIR/course_map_audit.md"
git commit -m "chore(audit): separate scaffold-only vs filled course maps ($DATE)"
git push
Optional: strict ‚Äútemplate similarity‚Äù detector
If you want a definitive list of files that are effectively the template (ignoring whitespace/blank lines) and nothing else:

# From repo root
BASE="curriculum/ontario/maps/secondary"
TEMPLATE="$BASE/_TEMPLATE_SECONDARY_MAP.md"
echo "Files identical to template (normalized):"
for f in "$BASE"/*.md; do
  [[ "$f" == "$TEMPLATE" ]] && continue
  if diff -q <(sed -E 's/[[:space:]]+$//; /^[[:space:]]*$/d' "$f") \
              <(sed -E 's/[[:space:]]+$//; /^[[:space:]]*$/d' "$TEMPLATE") >/dev/null; then
    echo "  ‚Ä¢ $f"
  fi
done
If you want, I can also wire a pre-commit check that blocks commits when a new map is still scaffold-only.

  # 1) Identical to template after trimming whitespace/blank lines?

  bytes=$(wc -c < "$f")

ChatGPT said:
Here‚Äôs the full scaffold for ENG2D ‚Äî Grade 10 Academic English, including verbatim Overall and Specific Expectations from the official Ontario curriculum. You can paste this directly into your ENG2D.md.

---
course: ENG2D
grade: 10
subject: English
stream: Academic
stage: 6
source_pdf: curriculum/ontario/pdfs/english910currb.pdf
---

# ENG2D ‚Äî English, Grade 10 (Academic)

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Oral Communication
- B. Reading and Literature Studies
- C. Writing
- D. Media Studies

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Oral Communication
By the end of this course, students will:
- listen to understand and respond appropriately in a variety of situations for a variety of purposes;
- use speaking skills and strategies appropriately to communicate with different audiences for a variety of purposes;
- reflect on and identify their strengths as listeners and speakers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful in oral communication situations; :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

### Strand B ‚Äî Reading and Literature Studies
By the end of this course, students will:
- read and demonstrate an understanding of a variety of literary, informational, and graphic texts, using a range of strategies to construct meaning;
- recognize a variety of text forms, text features, and stylistic elements and demonstrate understanding of how they help communicate meaning;
- use knowledge of words and cueing systems to read fluently;
- reflect on and identify their strengths as readers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful before, during, and after reading. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

### Strand C ‚Äî Writing
By the end of this course, students will:
- generate, gather, and organize ideas and information to write for an intended purpose and audience;
- draft and revise their writing, using a variety of forms and stylistic elements appropriate for the purpose and audience;
- use editing, proofreading, and publishing strategies and knowledge of conventions to present their work effectively;
- reflect on and identify their strengths as writers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful at different stages in the writing process. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

### Strand D ‚Äî Media Studies
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of a variety of media texts;
- identify media forms and explain how the conventions and techniques associated with them are used to create meaning;
- create a variety of media texts for different purposes and audiences using appropriate forms and techniques;
- describe strategies used in interpreting and creating media texts, explain which ones were helpful, and identify steps they can take to improve as media interpreters and producers. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

## 3) Specific Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Oral Communication
- A1.1 listen in order to understand and respond appropriately in a variety of situations for a variety of purposes;
- A1.2 use speaking skills and strategies appropriately to communicate with different audiences for a variety of purposes;
- A1.3 reflect on and identify their strengths as listeners and speakers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

### Strand B ‚Äî Reading and Literature Studies
- B1.1 read and demonstrate an understanding of a variety of literary, informational, and graphic texts, using a range of strategies to construct meaning;
- B1.2 recognize a variety of text forms, text features, and stylistic elements and demonstrate understanding of how they help communicate meaning;
- B1.3 use knowledge of words and cueing systems to read fluently;
- B1.4 reflect on and identify their strengths as readers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

### Strand C ‚Äî Writing
- C1.1 generate, gather, and organize ideas and information to write for an intended purpose and audience;
- C1.2 draft and revise writing, using a variety of forms and stylistic elements appropriate for the purpose and audience;
- C1.3 use editing, proofreading, and publishing strategies and conventions to present writing effectively;
- C1.4 reflect on and identify their strengths as writers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

### Strand D ‚Äî Media Studies
- D1.1 demonstrate understanding of a variety of media texts;
- D1.2 identify media forms and explain how their conventions create meaning;
- D1.3 create media texts for different purposes and audiences using appropriate forms and techniques;
- D1.4 describe strategies used in interpreting and creating media texts, explain which ones were helpful, and identify steps to improve as media interpreters and producers. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

## 4) Planning Tables

### 4.1 Worksheet Plan
| Expectation Code | Topic / Focus                  | Worksheet ID   | Versions | Notes |
|------------------|--------------------------------|----------------|----------|-------|
| A1.1‚ÄìA1.3        | Oral communication strategies  | WS-ENG10-001   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| B1.1‚ÄìB1.4        | Reading comprehension & fluency| WS-ENG10-002   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| C1.1‚ÄìC1.4        | Writing process & conventions  | WS-ENG10-003   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| D1.1‚ÄìD1.4        | Media analysis & production    | WS-ENG10-004   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |

### 4.2 Assessment Plan
| Assessment ID | Subject | Grade | Count | Strand Coverage | Notes                        |
|---------------|---------|-------|-------|-----------------|------------------------------|
| **AS-E10**    | English | 10    | 1     | Strands A‚ÄìD     | Culminating; diagnostic task |

**Strand Coverage**  
- A: A1.1‚ÄìA1.3  
- B: B1.1‚ÄìB1.4  
- C: C1.1‚ÄìC1.4  
- D: D1.1‚ÄìD1.4

Here‚Äôs the full scaffold with verbatim Overall and Specific Expectations from the Ontario curriculum:

---
course: ENG4U
grade: 12
subject: English
stream: University
stage: 6
source_pdf: curriculum/ontario/pdfs/english1112currb.pdf
---

# ENG4U ‚Äî English, Grade 12 (University)

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Oral Communication
- B. Reading and Literature Studies
- C. Writing
- D. Media Studies

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Oral Communication
By the end of this course, students will:
- listen in order to understand and respond appropriately in a variety of situations for a variety of purposes;
- use speaking skills and strategies appropriately to communicate with different audiences for a variety of purposes;
- reflect on and identify their strengths as listeners and speakers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful in oral communication situations.

### Strand B ‚Äî Reading and Literature Studies
By the end of this course, students will:
- read and demonstrate an understanding of a variety of complex literary, informational, and graphic texts, using a range of strategies to construct meaning;
- recognize a variety of text forms, text features, and stylistic elements and demonstrate understanding of how they help communicate meaning;
- use knowledge of words and cueing systems to read fluently;
- reflect on and identify their strengths as readers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful before, during, and after reading.

### Strand C ‚Äî Writing
By the end of this course, students will:
- generate, gather, and organize ideas and information to write for an intended purpose and audience;
- draft and revise their writing, using a variety of forms and stylistic elements appropriate for the purpose and audience;
- use editing, proofreading, and publishing strategies and knowledge of conventions to present their work effectively;
- reflect on and identify their strengths as writers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful at different stages in the writing process.

### Strand D ‚Äî Media Studies
By the end of this course, students will:
- demonstrate an understanding of a variety of media texts;
- identify media forms and explain how the conventions and techniques associated with them are used to create meaning;
- create a variety of media texts for different purposes and audiences using appropriate forms, conventions, and techniques;
- reflect on and identify their strengths as media interpreters and producers, areas for improvement, and the strategies they found most helpful.

## 3) Specific Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Oral Communication
- A1.1 listen to understand and interpret ideas and information in oral texts, including increasingly complex texts, accurately and fluently;
- A1.2 use speaking skills and strategies appropriately to communicate effectively in discussions and presentations;
- A1.3 reflect on and evaluate their strengths as listeners and speakers, and set goals for improvement.

### Strand B ‚Äî Reading and Literature Studies
- B1.1 read and interpret a variety of literary, informational, and graphic texts, using a range of strategies;
- B1.2 analyze text forms, features, and stylistic elements to explain how they help communicate meaning;
- B1.3 use knowledge of words and cueing systems to read fluently and accurately;
- B1.4 reflect on and evaluate their strengths as readers and set goals for improvement.

### Strand C ‚Äî Writing
- C1.1 generate, gather, and organize ideas and information to write for specific purposes and audiences;
- C1.2 draft and revise their writing, using a variety of literary and informational forms and stylistic elements appropriate for the purpose and audience;
- C1.3 use knowledge of conventions and strategies for editing, proofreading, and publishing to present their work effectively;
- C1.4 reflect on and evaluate their strengths as writers and set goals for improvement.

### Strand D ‚Äî Media Studies
- D1.1 demonstrate an understanding of a variety of media texts;
- D1.2 analyze how conventions and techniques are used in different media forms to communicate meaning;
- D1.3 create a variety of media texts for different purposes and audiences, using appropriate conventions and techniques;
- D1.4 reflect on and evaluate their strengths as media interpreters and producers and set goals for improvement.

## 4) Planning Tables

| C1.1‚ÄìC1.4        | Writing process & conventions     | WS-ENG12-003   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |
| D1.1‚ÄìD1.4        | Media analysis & production       | WS-ENG12-004   | vA‚ÄìvD    |       |

course: MDM4U

# MDM4U ‚Äî Mathematics of Data Management

## 1) Strands Overview
- A. Counting and Probability  
- B. Probability Distributions  
- C. Organization of Data for Analysis  
- D. Statistical Analysis  
- E. Culminating Data Management Investigation  

## 2) Overall Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Counting and Probability
By the end of this course, students will:
1. solve problems involving the probability of an event or a combination of events for discrete sample spaces;  
2. solve problems involving the application of permutations and combinations to determine the probability of an event. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

### Strand B ‚Äî Probability Distributions
By the end of this course, students will:
1. demonstrate an understanding of discrete probability distributions, represent them numerically, graphically, and algebraically, determine expected values, and solve related problems from a variety of applications;  
2. demonstrate an understanding of continuous probability distributions, make connections to discrete probability distributions, determine standard deviations, describe key features of the normal distribution, and solve related problems from a variety of applications. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

### Strand C ‚Äî Organization of Data for Analysis
By the end of this course, students will:
1. demonstrate an understanding of the role of data in statistical studies and the variability inherent in data, distinguish different types of data;  
2. describe the characteristics of a good sample, some sampling techniques, and principles of primary data collection, and collect and organize data to solve a problem. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

### Strand D ‚Äî Statistical Analysis
By the end of this course, students will:
1. analyse, interpret, and draw conclusions from one-variable data using numerical and graphical summaries;  
2. analyse, interpret, and draw conclusions from two-variable data using numerical, graphical, and algebraic summaries;  
3. demonstrate an understanding of the applications of data management used by the media and the advertising industry and in various occupations. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

### Strand E ‚Äî Culminating Data Management Investigation
By the end of this course, students will:
1. design and carry out a culminating investigation that requires the integration and application of the knowledge and skills related to the expectations of this course;  
2. communicate the findings of a culminating investigation and provide constructive critiques of the investigations of others. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

## 3) Specific Expectations

### Strand A ‚Äî Counting and Probability
- A1.1 solve problems involving the probability of an event for discrete sample spaces;  
- A1.2 solve problems involving combinations and permutations to determine probabilities.

### Strand B ‚Äî Probability Distributions
- B1.1 generate and represent probability distributions (discrete), calculate expected values, and solve related problems;  
- B1.2 describe and solve problems involving continuous distributions, including normal distribution and standard deviation.

### Strand C ‚Äî Organization of Data for Analysis
- C1.1 distinguish between types of data in statistical contexts;  
- C1.2 describe characteristics of a good sample, sampling techniques, and principles of primary data collection;  
- C1.3 collect and organize data to solve statistical problems.

### Strand D ‚Äî Statistical Analysis
- D1.1 analyse one-variable data using numerical and graphical summaries;  
- D1.2 analyse two-variable data using numerical, graphical, and algebraic summaries;  
- D1.3 explain how data management is applied in media, advertising, and occupation-related contexts.

### Strand E ‚Äî Culminating Data Management Investigation
- E1.1 design and carry out a culminating data investigation integrating course knowledge and skills;  
- E1.2 communicate findings and critique peer investigations.

## 4) Planning Tables

### 4.1 Worksheet Plan
| Expectation Code | Topic / Focus                     | Worksheet ID     | Versions | Notes                |
|------------------|-----------------------------------|------------------|----------|----------------------|
| A1.1‚ÄìA1.2        | Discrete probability & combinations | WS-MDM12-001     | vA‚ÄìvD    |                      |
| B1.1             | Discrete distributions & expectation | WS-MDM12-002     | vA‚ÄìvD    |                      |
| B1.2             | Continuous distributions & normal   | WS-MDM12-003     | vA‚ÄìvD    |                      |
| C1.1‚ÄìC1.3        | Sampling and data organization     | WS-MDM12-004     | vA‚ÄìvD    |                      |
| D1.1             | One-variable data analysis         | WS-MDM12-005     | vA‚ÄìvD    |                      |
| D1.2             | Two-variable data analysis         | WS-MDM12-006     | vA‚ÄìvD    |                      |
| D1.3             | Media & occupational applications  | WS-MDM12-007     | vA‚ÄìvD    |                      |
| E1.1‚ÄìE1.2        | Culminating investigation scaffold | WS-MDM12-008     | vA‚ÄìvD    |                      |

### 4.2 Assessment Plan
| Assessment ID | Subject     | Grade | Count | Strand Coverage       | Notes                           |
|---------------|-------------|-------|-------|-----------------------|---------------------------------|

course: MTH1W
